Bengbu

Discovery of Poisonous Smuggled Oil

Amidst the smuggling situation, various tax-evaded goods continue to be dumped southward, with white sugar and rayon being the most common. After strict inspections by various county authorities, they have gradually decreased. However, poisonous smuggled oil has recently been discovered in Shouxian, Yingshang, Tianjia'an and other places in northern Anhui. This smuggled oil is also extracted from soybeans. The oil's composition is mixed with human skin and bones, and although the toxicity is not severe, it still hinders hygiene when consumed. Moreover, the oil price is cheaper, and it is all trafficked and sold by ronin and traitors. This proves that it is smuggled oil without a doubt. After poisonous sugar, poisonous oil has emerged, which can also reveal the poisonous scheme of a certain country.

Anecdotes from a Southern Tour

Jiangshan: More People Than Land

—Special Correspondent Shi Ying

From Quzhou to Jiangshan, taking a morning bus, the green mountains and fields along the way offer endless beautiful scenery. The highway is built with gravel, and it can be driven on even in rainy weather. The Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway runs alongside it, and you can often see the race between cars and trains. The fact that the highway here is not planted with trees on either side suddenly reminded me of the highways in southern Zhejiang. On both sides, "I ask about the willows, I ask about the paulownia," and "the car speeds through," often revealing a few acres of lotus ponds through the willow gaps, like driving on the Su Causeway in West Lake. I don't feel any of the fatigue of the journey. After a while, I arrived in Jiangshan, checked into the Dachang Hotel in the city, which was renovated from a temple. The roof is high and airy, suitable for summer living. There is also the Jiangshan Hotel, which is also very old. The rest are mostly small inns. There is not even a good bathhouse in the entire city.

Twenty-five kilometers south of Jiangshan city is Mount Jianglang, and on the mountain are the Three Stone Peaks, standing tall and reaching into the sky, all several hundred feet high, visible from below but unclimbable. The county gets its name from this. On the outskirts of the city are also Rooster Mountain and Tiger Mountain, which are also several strange large stones piled on top of the mountains, like a rooster's comb and a crouching tiger (actually, they look very much like the humps and heads of crouching camels). Looking up in the city, you can just see their similar parts, that is, the rooster's head and the tiger's head and tail, protruding and receding on the eaves and corners of the streets. The people of Jiangshan are strong and fierce, and cases of robbery and murder occur almost every day. Especially during the hot summer, there are often tragic events of bandits being executed. The county government dares not place rickshaws in front of its door, for fear that they will be called to pull criminals to the execution ground. Feng Shui masters attribute this to the bad appearance of Tiger Mountain. Although many people are superstitious, in reality, these strange mountains and rocks have no eyes and are in the wrong place, so they suffer injustice.

Jiangshan, as a remote and small county, has an exceptionally large number of lawsuits. This is a fact. According to the person in charge of the local court, since the court was established in 1928, over one hundred cases have been transferred from the county government, some of which have been pending for more than two years without being tried, which is truly unjust. Statistics on the number of lawsuits accepted each year have increased from over one thousand cases to around one thousand five hundred cases. On average, more than four cases are accepted every day, and the cases of bandits and Red Pill criminals that are transferred to the county government for trial are not included. If we combine and analyze them, the first category is robbery, accounting for 40 percent (according to the county magistrate, it has gradually increased to 60 percent). The second category is assault, accounting for 30 percent. The third category is deprivation of freedom, accounting for 20 percent. The fourth category is Red Pill criminals, accounting for 10 percent. In addition, there are only two communist criminals who endanger the Republic. It can be seen that very few criminals aim to endanger national public safety, while robbery crimes of an economic nature account for more than half. The reasons for the second category of assault crimes are mostly due to rent and debt collection, so it can be said that most of them are for livelihood issues. The motives for other various crimes are also inevitably directly or indirectly related to livelihood issues.

At present, Jiangshan has two hundred people in prison in the county government and two hundred and eighty in the court, excluding the eighty or so on parole, totaling nearly four hundred. The limited prison is holding an increasing number of criminals, and problems often arise in management and supply. In addition, ignorant and foolish people are occasionally caught in the legal net, or are incited by malicious criminals, becoming increasingly depraved, or die in prison due to the spread of disease. It is said that the number is not small. This remote and small county has so many criminals, and observing the future, there is a crisis that will only worsen. The following briefly describes the situation, hoping that society will pay attention to it.

The main reasons for this problem are: first, the people are relatively strong and fierce. This is undeniable. During the severe drought two years ago, Zhejiang was shocked by the news of farmers forcing the county magistrate to pay respects to the City God to pray for rain. Later, they even smashed the Party headquarters and dragged the chairman of the Farmers' Association out to bake in the sun - this farcical drama was played by the people of Jiangshan. A few years ago, there was a rice shortage, and the farmers also flocked to the county government to coerce them. At that time, a new county magistrate surnamed Mi, who had just taken office for one day, was forced to say angrily, "I am only surnamed Mi, and I did not bring rice with me. The rice is in the rice shop, what are you doing here?" So they robbed all the rice shops, and the county magistrate Mi was immediately removed from his post due to the rice problem. The masses are so strong, and private individuals are not weak either. In the southeast two townships, especially in the twenty-seventh township and eighteen fortresses, there are so-called "cultivating" and "robbing" farmer bandits. For example, if there are four brothers, two or three have already been executed for robbery, and the rest still want to engage in that adventurous business without capital. At least they also want to kill the person who reported the crime.

Second, the arrowhead boats in the Qiantang River used to be mostly from Jiangshan. There are 10,000 households of boatmen, who navigate and transport goods here. There are also often four or five thousand porters who distribute goods to Fujian, Jiangxi, and Anhui provinces. Wild bamboo grows lush and green on the four mountains, and residents rely on papermaking for a living. There are over one hundred paper mills, employing one thousand and several hundred workers. In total, there are five or six thousand boatmen, porters, and paper workers. Now, due to the development of transportation, boatmen and porters are completely unemployed, and paper workers have also been idle for many years due to the loss of the Northeast market. "Only when clothing and food are sufficient do people know etiquette and righteousness; only when the granaries are full do they know honor and shame." Among this large group of unemployed people, there are naturally many who are the protagonists of increasing robbery.

Third, the total population of the county is 290,000, but there are only 300,000 mu of cultivated land, averaging only 1.23 mu per person, less than the minimum of 3 mu per person. With so few producers and so many consumers, it is no wonder that they are trapped in an environment where "in good years, they suffer all their lives, and in bad years, they cannot avoid robbery." Usually, when renting land, the landlords get 60 percent, and the tenants get only 40 percent. Because there is little land and many people, they have to compete for planting to make a living. In recent years, the implementation of the 25% rent reduction (that is, the tenant farmers take 25% of the harvest first, and then divide the rest equally with the landlord, so the tenants get 62.5% and the landlord gets 37.5%) has been very helpful to ordinary semi-self-cultivating farmers and tenant farmers. The attitude of the farmers in the formerly bandit-ridden areas has fortunately improved as a result. However, the food shortage cannot be compensated for. According to Mr. Song Rilong of the Party Committee, who recently returned from inspections in the twenty-seventh township (120 li from the city) and other places, "Only 5% of the villages eat rice, 45% eat sweet potatoes and other coarse grains, and the remaining 50% gather wild grass (also known as bitter leaves) to cook and eat." This is solid evidence.

Analyzing and summarizing the above three reasons, "more people than land" can be said to be the root cause. Looking at the history of one period of peace and one period of chaos, it is based on the population and land problem. When the cultivated land is vast and the population is sparse, the farmers are well-fed and clothed, and the "world is at peace." Later, due to the rapid increase in population and insufficient cultivated land allocation, people feel increasingly lacking in food, and when they encounter famine, vagrant bandits arise, and the "world is in great chaos," killing people in cities and fields. Until the death of most of the population, people are tired of chaos, and outstanding talents emerge to correct the chaos, allowing the surviving people to divide the remaining land of most of the dead, work hard and harvest, and the picture of prosperity and peace returns. In the future, with the progress of science and the improvement of farming systems, it is not yet certain that this cyclical tragedy will not be repeated. However, the current crisis of "more people than land" in Jiangshan is very terrifying. The so-called strong and fierce people are whipped and forged by the whip of bitter life. As for the unemployed group's helplessness, it is even more because the living space is too narrow to be accommodated. These are all obvious facts. The only way to solve this problem is to "implement an immigration policy." Hengfeng and Yiyang in eastern Jiangxi and Pucheng and Jian'ou in northern Fujian are mostly recovered red areas. Often, dozens or hundreds of miles of good farmland are still barren today. If immigrants are brought from Jiangshan, they can arrive in the evening after starting in the morning. I hope that the authorities will not just talk about it and implement it as soon as possible.

Local News

Reorganization of Guangdong Province Finances: Key Officials Depart for Guangdong Yesterday; Song Zi-liang and Others Fly to Shaoguan to Meet Yu Hanmou; Tang Ju and Li Cheng Convey Financial Secretary Kong's Instructions; Each Speaks on Their Assigned Mission Before Departure

Key officials specially appointed by the Ministry of Finance to reorganize the finances, financial institutions, monetary system, and taxes of Guangdong Province, including the newly appointed Special Commissioner of Finance for Guangdong Province and Director of the Department of Finance, Song Zi-liang; Zou Lin, Director of Political Affairs of the Ministry of Finance, representing Financial Secretary Kong to inspect and convey the Central Government's intention to reduce the burden on the people of Guangdong Province; Wu Jiantao, the newly appointed Director of the Guangdong-Guangxi Inter-regional Consolidated Tax Bureau; and Zhou Shouliang, Deputy Director of the Business Bureau of the Central Bank, departed yesterday morning at 8:00 AM on a specially chartered China National Aviation Corporation Douglas aircraft "Nanjing." Tang Shumin, General Manager of the Bank of Communications; Bei Songsun, Manager of the Shanghai Branch of the Bank of China; and Li Tisheng, Deputy Director of the Treasury Bureau of the Central Bank, departed yesterday morning at 10:00 AM on the Norddeutscher Lloyd steamer "Bremen." Financial Secretary Kong arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing yesterday morning to provide instructions to the officials. Meeting Kong Before Departure

Kong Xiangxi, President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance, had just returned to Nanjing from Shanghai on the evening of the 20th. After presiding over the Executive Yuan's routine meeting on the morning of the previous day on behalf of President Chiang, he rushed to take the 11:00 PM express train from Nanjing to Shanghai the night before, as he needed to give final instructions to Mr. Zhu and others. He arrived at the Zhenru Station at 6:50 AM yesterday morning and went directly to his private residence on the Avenue Road. Song, Zou, Tang, Bei, Zhou, and Li immediately went to see him to ask for instructions. Financial Secretary Kong gave them detailed instructions and offered words of encouragement. After talking for half an hour, Mr. Song and others left and went to the airport and wharf to depart. Subsequently, Financial Secretary Kong went to the Central Bank to work around 11:00 AM and is scheduled to fly to Xunyang this morning, then proceed to Lushan to escape the summer heat and meet with President Chiang to discuss important public matters.

Meeting Yu in Shaoguan

When Mr. Song and his party passed through Shaoguan, they disembarked briefly to meet with the newly appointed Pacification Commissioner of Guangdong, Yu Hanmou, to discuss everything before flying to Guangdong. After Mr. Song and others departed by plane yesterday morning, Chen Xing, Deputy Governor of the Central Bank, immediately telegraphed Guangzhou to notify Tang Haian, the newly appointed Salt Transport Commissioner of Guangdong and Guangxi, who had already transferred to Guangdong via Hong Kong, to inform all parties that Mr. Song and others were expected to arrive in Guangdong after 2:00 PM and to welcome them at the airport at that time.

Song Zi-liang (left) and Zou Lin (right) (International Press Photo)

Statements by Song and Zou

Song Zi-liang said, "Guangdong Province is my hometown. I am honored to be appointed by the government to reorganize its finances. However, my role is primarily to assist. I have not yet divested myself of my duties in the China Construction Bank and the National Goods Bank in Shanghai and will need to return to Shanghai in the future." Zou Lin said, "This trip is on behalf of Financial Secretary Kong to inspect and convey the Central Government's intention to sympathize with the people of Guangdong. My return date will be determined based on the completion of the work. A written statement will be issued in the future."

Statement by Wu Jiantao

Mr. Wu Jiantao flew to Nanjing from Jiangxi the day before yesterday and came to Shanghai by train with Financial Secretary Kong that night. He arrived yesterday morning and traveled with Mr. Song and others. According to Mr. Wu, he received the telegrammed order the day before yesterday and rushed to come without adequate preparation. His position as Director of the Jiangxi Provincial Department of Finance is temporarily being held by Liu Tigan, the Secretary-General of the provincial government, and he has not been able to relinquish it. His new position as Director of the Guangdong-Guangxi-Fujian Inter-regional Consolidated Tax Bureau is only a concurrent appointment. He will need to return to Jiangxi in about two months. Regarding the plan to reorganize the consolidated tax in Guangdong Province, he will decide after arriving in Guangdong and assessing the current situation. What can be reported at this time is that the general direction will be to maintain the original framework while increasing the strength of new personnel to strive for improvement.

Statement by Tang Shumin

According to Tang, the Ministry of Finance has appointed Song Zi-liang as Special Commissioner and Director of the Department of Finance to reorganize the finances of Guangdong Province, and a reorganization plan has already been determined. He and Bei Songsun are going to Guangdong to inspect the financial institutions of Guangdong Province and to find ways to reform the monetary system of Guangdong Province to complete the implementation of the legal tender policy. As for reforming the silver dollar system, the principle has long been decided and is imperative. How to reform it will be decided after arriving in Guangdong. The date of returning to Shanghai has not yet been determined.

Statement by Zhou Shouliang

According to Zhou, he and Li Tisheng were ordered to go to Guangdong to investigate the financial situation of Guangdong Province and plan to return to Shanghai in the short term. The plan to establish a Guangzhou branch of the Central Bank has already been decided, but specific measures will be determined after arriving in Guangdong. These measures will be implemented after being approved by the head office. He has requested leave from the Ministry of Transportation for his concurrent position at the Postal Remittances Bureau, which has been approved.

Chen Xing's Statement

According to Mr. Chen, the establishment of a Guangzhou branch of the Central Bank and a Guangzhou branch of the Issuing Reserve Management Committee is imperative. However, at the beginning of the establishment, the monetary system must first be unified. Everything will be implemented as soon as possible after Director Zou and Mr. Tang and Bei return north after their inspection and investigation and the measures are decided. It is understood that there is already an Issuing Management Committee in Guangzhou, and this time it will simply be reorganized to be directly under Shanghai. The selection of committee members will largely remain the same, with Zou Minchu and others continuing to serve. As for the silver in Guangdong Province, it is reported to be 100 million yuan in silver dollars, equivalent to 98 million legal tender yuan.

Chen Guangfu Speaks

Denies Sino-American and Sino-Philippine Agreements

Reuter's Shanghai, July 22 - Reports in the Japanese press that a recent Sino-American monetary agreement includes continued loans to China and the purchase of war materials have been solemnly denied today by Chen Guangfu, the chief Chinese negotiator of the agreement. Mr. Chen is the General Manager of the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank and a senior advisor to the Ministry of Finance. He told a Reuter's reporter that his mission to Washington was solely to discuss monetary issues with officials of the U.S. Treasury. As a result of the discussions, the U.S. Treasury has agreed to purchase a large quantity of silver from China to further strengthen China's newly stabilized currency. Mr. Chen also clarified that this measure is purely a commercial transaction and has no political nature whatsoever. Mr. Chen also denied reports that he and Guo Bingwen negotiated a commercial agreement with the Philippines during their recent return to China from the United States. He said that while he did visit President Quezon, the talks were purely social in nature and did not involve Sino-Philippine commercial issues.

Twenty-One Chambers of Commerce Telegraph, Requesting Postponement of Income Tax; Income Tax Should Be Implemented on the Day That Disguised Likin is Abolished

The representatives of twenty-one provincial, municipal, and county chambers of commerce holding a meeting at the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce received a telegram from the Hankou Municipal Chamber of Commerce. After deliberation at the joint conference, a telegram was sent to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance requesting postponement of income tax. The original telegram is as follows:

Telegram from Hankou

Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Greetings: Recently received a telegram from the Wuxian Chamber of Commerce stating that the provisional regulations on income tax are awaiting amendment and implementation. At this time of widespread poverty and financial exhaustion, implementation should be postponed to allow for a brief respite. Please maintain a consistent stance, etc. Submitted to the 32nd executive committee meeting of this chamber of commerce today, all members agreed that industry and commerce are declining, all sectors are withering, and the national economy is on the verge of bankruptcy. All stores are barely maintaining their current status, and those that have not yet collapsed are fortunate enough. Where is there income to speak of? Government officials are not thinking of showing compassion and fostering vitality, but want to forcibly implement income tax. The people are exhausted and cannot even save themselves, how can they bear this heavy burden? The situation is the same everywhere as it is in this city. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce is currently inviting fifteen provincial and municipal chambers of commerce to discuss anti-smuggling. It is imperative to telegraph based on the telegram from the Wuxian Chamber of Commerce, submit a special case for discussion, propose to fight vigorously, and telegraph our chamber of commerce's attending representatives Yu Rongqiao and others to explain the reasons for the proposal and to implement the proposal to achieve the goal of postponing implementation, etc. Recorded in the minutes. Specially record the case and telegram to your chamber of commerce. Please submit for discussion and forward to our chamber of commerce representatives Yu Rongqiao and others for reference. Hankou Municipal Chamber of Commerce Ke.

Joint Telegram to Nanjing

Executive Yuan, Ministry of Finance, Greetings: Our chamber of commerce, etc., received an invitation from the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to assist in anti-smuggling and to address the issue of amending the Chambers of Commerce Law and the Guild Law. A joint conference was held in Shanghai on Ke day. Today, a telegram was received from the Hankou Municipal Chamber of Commerce stating (telegram text above). After being submitted for discussion, all members agreed that although income tax is a good tax, when a good tax is implemented, bad taxes should also be abolished. The National Government clearly ordered the abolition of likin many years ago, but many provinces still have disguised likin, such as the Jiangxi Clearance of Bandits and Post-Disaster Donations, the Zhejiang Silk Improvement Fee, the Hunan Production and Sales Tax, the Guangdong Special Tax, the Sichuan Landing Tax, the Guangxi Military Contribution, and the Shaanxi, Gansu, and Yunnan Special Consumption Tax, with countless different names. Whether it is native goods or machine-made domestic products, there is repeated collection, and no one is spared. The tax rate is even ten times higher than the previous likin. While demanding that merchants bear legal burdens, provinces should not be allowed to retain the dregs of likin. This is the first point. Since the business tax was introduced, the business tax bureaus in various provinces have been unable to determine the standard for total business revenue, resulting in frequent disputes with merchants and strikes. Now, in addition to the total business revenue, they must also examine the net profit. The accounting systems of merchants are not standardized, especially in the interior, and there are even those who only show a surplus on paper at the end of each year to please shareholders. If this is regarded as net profit and taxed accordingly, the disputes will be ten times greater than now. This is the second point. Reports state that foreigners will also be taxed equally under the income tax, but as exemplified by the recent agreement on factory inspections in concessions, it can be seen that they will rely on their extraterritorial rights and will not be able to tax foreigners in the future. Taking the example of the Shanghai concessions, which still cannot levy business tax, it can be seen that the introduction of income tax will not only be unable to tax foreigners, but also the merchants in the concessions. The result will only be to drive fish into the deep and fuel the prosperity of the concessions, leading to capital flight. This is the third point. Based on the first point above, the central government must strictly supervise and urge the provinces to abolish likin. Income tax should be implemented on the day that disguised likin is abolished. Merchants can then get a reprieve. Based on the second point above, the authorities must also negotiate on the diplomatic front and ensure that foreigners and concessions are taxed equally. This is necessary to avoid significant damage to national welfare and livelihoods. It was resolved to request the government to postpone the implementation of income tax until the above procedures are fully completed. When the above issues are resolved one by one and it is possible to implement the tax, all matters related to the implementation methods and detailed rules should also be discussed and finalized with the business community in order to ensure the best possible outcome and avoid conflicts. There is a precedent for the previous likin abolition conference. In addition to the accounting system, the attending representatives will discuss the national accounting system improvement plan in detail. Urgently record the case and telegram to be submitted for review. We hope that our request will be approved. We are extremely eager to hear back. The Joint Association of Chambers of Commerce of the seven provinces of Hubei, Henan, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Guangdong, and Jiangxi, and the fourteen municipal and county chambers of commerce of Nanjing, Qingdao, Shanghai, Hankou, Jinan, Zhenjiang, Guangzhou, Nanchang, Kaifeng, Changsha, Taiyuan, Wuhu, Hangzhou, and Minhou bow down. This document borrows and affixes the seal of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce. This is stated in combination.

Grain, Oil, and Cake Industries Donate to Buy Plane for Birthday

Decision to Donate 100,000 Yuan, Detailed Rules Approved

The Shanghai Committee for the China Aviation Association's Expanded National Aviation Salvation Movement to Raise Funds to Purchase Aircraft and Present Them to the Government for Chiang Kai-shek's Fiftieth Birthday Celebration Committee recently received a letter from the Shanghai Grain, Oil, and Cake Industries Association, stating that Generalissimo Chiang swore an oath to launch the Northern Expedition, laid the foundation for China, eradicated the communists, and saved the people. His great achievements will be eternally remembered by the party and the country. This year marks his fiftieth birthday, and this association, in order to express its support, has repeatedly convened meetings and decided to levy a donation on goods from the industry to purchase an aircraft and present it to the government. Detailed rules for various goods donations have been drafted and a date for commencement has been set. The committee has submitted the letter to the Shanghai Municipal Government for approval and filing, and has also sent it to various sectors for reference. The detailed rules are as follows: Detailed Rules for the Shanghai Grain, Oil, and Cake Industries Association's Collection of Donations to Purchase Aircraft for Birthday Celebration: 1. Donations will be collected on all goods operated by members of this association until 100,000 yuan has been collected to purchase an aircraft. 2. Foreign goods, rice, wheat, grains, peanuts, sesame, rapeseed, etc., will be levied at one cent per dan of the quoted price, with the buyer and seller each paying five li. 3. Oils such as soybean oil, rapeseed oil, and raw oil will be levied at two cents per dan of the quoted price, with the buyer and seller each paying one cent. 4. River rice mills will be levied at one cent per shi of the quoted price, with the buyer and seller each paying five li. 5. Cakes: Soybean cakes will be levied at two li per piece, with the buyer and seller each paying one li. Rapeseed cakes, mung bean cakes, and peanut cakes will be levied at four li per unit of the quoted price, with the buyer and seller each paying two li. 6. Sellers should request receipts from buyers, collect them, and submit them to this association. Buyers should submit the stubs to this association for review and collection. 7. If the buyer and seller attempt to avoid payment without following these detailed rules, they will be severely punished once discovered. 8. If a Hakka attempts to avoid payment and sells directly to merchants without joining the association, once discovered, in addition to the association compensating the same industry for the corresponding losses, the official authorities should immediately be requested to impose severe sanctions. 9. These detailed rules will be submitted to the municipal government for approval and implementation. 10. If there are any matters not covered in these detailed rules, they may be amended at any time with approval. Various dance halls are enthusiastically holding entertainment events, and the income will be transferred to donate to purchase aircraft for birthday celebration. The Old Dahua Dance Hall donated all of its income on the 20th, totaling 153.25 national currency yuan, which has already been handed over, and the Aircraft Purchase Commemoration Association has received the receipt. It is reported that the Shengli, Paris, Haoyou, and Mingxing dance halls will also hold events on a regular basis.

After Yesterday's Third General Meeting, the Chamber of Commerce Joint Conference Concluded. Petitions to Amend Partnership Liability in the Morning, and Committee Members of the Anti-Smuggling Federation Elected in the Afternoon. Representatives of Various Associations Will Petition in the Capital Tomorrow.

After the opening of the joint conference of chambers of commerce from various provinces and cities, at 10 a.m. yesterday, the presidium, including Wang Xiaolai, visited Sun Ke, the President of the Legislative Yuan, to petition for the amendment of partnership liability. At 11 a.m., the third general meeting was held, with 36 representatives from various provinces and cities attending. They passed the review report of the commercial law group's proposals and revised the organizational outline of the Anti-Smuggling Federation. At 3 p.m., the meeting continued, and 27 committee members of the Anti-Smuggling Federation were elected. It was resolved to establish the All-China Federation of Chambers of Commerce, and the presidium led the chambers of commerce of 21 provinces, cities, and counties to each nominate a representative to gather in Beijing yesterday morning to petition the Central Party Headquarters and other authorities. Details are recorded as follows:

Visiting President Sun

At 10 a.m. yesterday, the presidium, consisting of Wang Xiaolai, Yu Rongqiao, Cai Chang, Yuan Duanfu, Yu Xiaochuan, and others, went to Columbia Road to visit Sun Ke, the President of the Legislative Yuan, to petition for the amendment of Article 681 of the Civil Code regarding joint and several liability for partnership businesses. Wang and others stated that the provision was incompatible with commercial practices and difficult to apply in practice, and indirectly contributed to the decline of commerce. Sun agreed to accept the petition and have the Yuan discuss it in detail, and the petition will be sent directly to the Legislative Yuan. The original petition is recorded as follows: Presented to the President, regarding the petition. It has been found that Article 681 of the Debt Section of the Civil Code stipulates that partners bear unlimited joint and several liability. Chambers of Commerce in various provinces believe that this provision is greatly at odds with national conditions and commercial practices, and they have been constantly petitioning for its amendment. The Yuan is requested to respect commercial sentiment and adopt a compromise. There was a proposal by eight legislators, including Wu Kaixian, to enact a Commercial Registration Law as a remedy. Article 9 of the draft law stipulates that partners who register their names, addresses, and capital contributions shall be liable for sharing losses within the limit of their capital contributions. The point of contention over the years could have been resolved, but ultimately, due to the disagreement between the Civil Law Committee and the Commercial Law Committee of the Yuan, the draft law has been stalled since October of the 23rd year. The present delegations attended the joint conference in Shanghai to discuss the tax system and amendment of the Chamber of Commerce Law. In reviewing this, it was decided that if the draft law is stalled because the Commercial Registration Law is a procedural law and the Civil Law is a substantive law, and a procedural law cannot change a substantive law, then the only way to thoroughly remedy the situation is to incorporate the full text of Article 9 of the draft law into Article 681 of the Civil Code as an exception to the second paragraph, and add a sentence at the end of the second paragraph stating that a registration procedure will be separately defined. In this way, there is no contradiction between Article 681 of the Debt Section of the Civil Code and the Commercial Registration Law, and the legislative style will be more harmonious. If the only reason is to protect creditor's rights and the method of joint and several liability is insisted upon without any change, then the principle of equal protection for creditors and debtors should be adopted, and this action would not benefit creditors but would only encourage the bad habit of evasion. Chambers of Commerce in various provinces have pointed out the advantages and disadvantages in previous resolutions and dispatches in great detail. If this system is not changed, it will make accounts even more difficult to collect, and commercial ethics will further deteriorate, sinking deeper and becoming more difficult to remedy. The representatives of this delegation are in the commercial world and are well aware of the advantages and disadvantages. Creditor's rights and debts alternate, and it is by no means a one-sided calculation. In order to protect this century-old precedent, we hereby jointly present this petition to the President for consideration. Regarding partnership debt, whether starting with amending Article 681 of the Debt Section of the Civil Code, or maintaining the original proposal to enact a Commercial Registration Law as a remedy, we request a prompt decision to provide a basis for merchants to relieve the desires of merchants over the years, which would be greatly appreciated. Furthermore, this matter is being stamped with the seal of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the venue of the meeting, and we hereby make a joint statement. Respectfully presented to Sun, President of the Legislative Yuan.

Third General Meeting

At 11 a.m. yesterday, the third general meeting was held. The presidium consisted of Wang Xiaolai, Yu Rongqiao, Cai Chang, Yuan Ruifu, Yu Xiaochuan, and others. After the formalities, Wang Xiaolai gave a report, and then the discussion began. (1) Discussed the draft organizational outline of the Anti-Smuggling Federation, and it was resolved to amend and pass it. (2) Discussed the proposal of the commercial law group, and the review committee of the commercial law group's proposal reported. Resolved: Five review reports passed. The meeting adjourned at 12 noon. The representatives of the chambers of commerce from various provinces and cities were invited to a banquet at the Hua'an Building on Jing'an Temple Road by the National Association of Accountants and the Shanghai Association of Accountants. At 2 p.m., the meeting continued to discuss the following matters: (1) Amended the fourth article of the organizational outline of the Anti-Smuggling Federation passed in the morning to read: "Each of the above departments shall have one director, appointed by the federation from among the committee members, and one deputy director, appointed by the committee members." (2) Elected 27 committee members of the Anti-Smuggling Federation. (3) Discussed the temporary proposal by nine representatives, including Jia Shaowu, Liang Jingxuan, Yao Zilun, Lin Chuanshen, Wang Yungu, Tao Yutang, Huang Xiren, Ke Ganchen, and Jin Runxiang, to improve the organization of the All-China Federation of Chambers of Commerce. Resolved: The provincial chambers of commerce of the seven provinces and the representatives of the three special municipal chambers of commerce attending this joint meeting shall legally initiate the organization of the All-China Federation of Chambers of Commerce. (4) Discussed the two outlines of the organizational work of the anti-smuggling committees of local chambers of commerce. Resolved: Handed over to the Anti-Smuggling Federation to formulate and implement them promptly. (5) Discussed the proposal to send representatives to Beijing to petition the relevant authorities separately regarding the resolutions of this joint meeting. Resolved: The presidium shall lead each of the 21 provinces, cities, and county chambers of commerce to nominate one representative to go to Beijing to petition the Central Party Headquarters, the two Yuan of the Executive and Legislative branches, and the two ministries of Finance and Industry separately, and it was scheduled to gather at the Nanjing Municipal Chamber of Commerce at 9 a.m. on the 24th. After the discussion, the chairman delivered a closing speech and the meeting adjourned.

Anti-Smuggling Outline

Organizational Outline of the All-China Anti-Smuggling Federation of Chambers of Commerce: (1) This federation is organized by chambers of commerce from various regions. (2) The purpose of this federation is to assist the government, guide local chambers of commerce in investigating tax evasion and smuggled goods, and safeguard the transportation and sale of legitimate goods. (3) This federation shall be composed of 27 representatives mutually elected by chambers of commerce from various regions to form a committee, which shall elect 7 standing committee members to form a standing committee to handle daily affairs. (4) This federation shall establish the following departments: 1. General Affairs Department, 2. Intelligence Department, 3. Organization Department, 4. Statistics Department. Each of the above departments shall have one director and one deputy director, appointed by the federation from among the committee members. 5. The meeting schedule of this federation shall be divided into: 1. General Committee Meeting, convened every three months; 2. Standing Committee Meeting, convened every two weeks. Special meetings may be convened as necessary. 6. This federation shall have one secretary and several staff members, appointed by the Standing Committee, and shall direct their work. 7. The expenses of this federation shall be shared by the chambers of commerce in various regions, set at 5 to 20 yuan per month per association. 8. The address of this federation shall be within the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce. 9. Local chambers of commerce shall organize anti-smuggling committees, named "Anti-Smuggling Committee of [Location] Chamber of Commerce." Their regulations shall be formulated separately. 10. Detailed rules for this federation and its departments shall be formulated separately. 11. This outline shall be implemented upon passage by the meeting of representatives of chambers of commerce from various regions, and shall be reported to the relevant government authorities for record. The same shall apply to amendments.

Commercial Law Proposal

The review process of the commercial law group's proposals was reported by Deputy Director Luo Xiaohua as follows: The commercial law group received a total of 12 proposals from the Zhejiang Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce, Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce, Wuhu Chamber of Commerce, Haimen Chamber of Commerce, and others, including (1) 4 proposals regarding mandatory membership, (2) 2 proposals regarding arrears in membership fees, (3) 1 proposal regarding increasing the number of committee members, (4) 1 proposal regarding the term of committee members, (5) 4 proposals regarding supplementary articles. Review opinions: Regarding items (1) and (2), the following measures are proposed: (1) Petition the government to amend the current commercial organization laws and regulations to clearly define the organizational system of commercial organizations. (2) When amending laws and regulations, accept the opinions of commercial organizations as much as possible and send representatives to state them. (3) If trade associations fail to join the Chamber of Commerce as members, or join but fail to fulfill all obligations, report to the competent authorities for reorganization or restructuring. If the staff are negligent in performing their duties, report to the competent authorities for administrative punishment. (4) If companies and firms fail to send representatives to join the guild as members, the guild should set a deadline for them to complete the above procedures. If they fail to comply after the deadline, or join but fail to fulfill all obligations, the Chamber of Commerce should report to the competent authorities to impose a fine in accordance with the Administrative Execution Law and still order them to join the association. If they still fail to comply after the deadline, their business should be suspended. Regarding item 3, it is proposed to appropriately increase the number of executive and supervisory committee members. Article 18 of the Chamber of Commerce Law should be amended as follows: The executive committee members and supervisory committee members of the Chamber of Commerce shall be elected by the members' meeting from among the members' representatives. The number of executive committee members shall be from seven to forty-five, and the number of supervisory committee members shall be from three to twenty-one, as approved by the competent government agency based on the complexity of the Chamber of Commerce's affairs. The executive committee members mentioned above may mutually elect standing committee members and elect one person from among the standing committee members as chairman. Regarding (4) extending the term of committee members, it is proposed to temporarily retain it. Regarding (5) supplementing the articles of the Chamber of Commerce Law and the Trade Association Law, (A) Haimen Chamber of Commerce: (1) Please amend the first item of Article 8 of the Chamber of Commerce Law regarding the elimination of qualifications, which states "deprivation of public rights" should be changed to "criminal punishment." It is proposed to pass it. (2) Please delete the clause "Store members must be registered according to law." It is proposed to change "registered" to "recorded." (B) Zhejiang Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce: (1) Amend Article 9 of the Chamber of Commerce's duties and move the original Article 9 to Article 10. It is proposed to delete the word "matters" in Article 9 and change "direct" to "guide." (2) Add a new Article 11 to restrict the method for members to withdraw from the association, and (3) amend the text of Article 4. It is proposed to pass all of them. (C) Zhejiang Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce: (1) Amend the Trade Association Law to allow more than seven companies in the same industry to organize an association. It is proposed to pass it in conjunction with item 1 of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce's proposal. (2) The word "Chamber of Commerce" should be added to the documents submitted by the association to the subjective authorities. It is proposed to pass it. (D) The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce proposed three measures to improve the organization of merchant groups. It is proposed to move (1) to (2), appropriately amend Article 9, and add an item as the second item. Regarding the proposed amendment of item (1) of the guild, it is proposed to pass it. It is proposed to list item (2) separately. It is proposed to pass item (3). However, due to the addition of an item, the original second item added to Article 7 is changed to Article 8, second item. In addition, the mandatory membership part is handled according to the methods proposed in cases (1) and (2). Are the above review opinions appropriate? Please make a decision. Director Zhu Yaoting, Deputy Director Luo Qinghua.

Anti-Smuggling Committee Members

The list of 27 committee members of the All-China Anti-Smuggling Federation of Chambers of Commerce is as follows: Luo Huizong, Gao Bochang, Yu Ting, Zheng Longwen, Yu Xiaochuan, Cheng Ganqing, Xu Guosen, Yuan Duanfu, Gu Sumin, Cai Chang, Wan Zhucun, Liang Rendao, Zhu Yaoting, Jia Shaowu, Yuan Yousheng, Zhang Shuliang, Liu Wenting, Chen Xinyan, Tao Yutang, Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, Xu Jiyun, Jin Runxiang, Ke Ganchen, Ge Jechen, Xu Shufen, Luo Yuming.

Closing Remarks

Chairman Wang Xiaoxiang delivered a closing speech, saying, "This meeting was convened during the height of summer and on short notice. However, we still had representatives from seven provincial federations of chambers of commerce and fourteen city and county chambers of commerce. Originally, there are countless matters that chambers of commerce should discuss together, but considering the priority and urgency, we have focused our discussion on the tax system and the amendment of commercial laws and regulations to avoid being overly broad and building castles in the air. Since the proposals are concentrated on the above two cases, the matters to be discussed during the three-day meeting have been largely clarified. For example, regarding the issue of assisting in anti-smuggling, it has been decided to establish a national anti-smuggling federation to unify methods and facilitate communication. What should be strived for in the future is 'how to do' rather than 'how to say.' In addition, those that have a stake in the tax system and merchants are requesting the government to cut off all disguised surcharges in various provinces and to point out the three major prerequisites that should be paid attention to when starting an income tax and to ask them to adopt it. This matter still requires the national business community to continue to appeal to the government with a consistent spirit. This meeting is only the beginning. Regarding how to amend the Chamber of Commerce Law and the Trade Association Law, this meeting has summarized the opinions of all parties and prepared articles for submission to the legislative authorities for adoption. The time for the realization of this matter is not far off, as the environment has changed, and the claims of the legislative authorities and the business community are now consistent. As for the issue of the quick-liability of partnerships in shops, merchants have been requesting amendments for years, but the compromise proposed by the Legislative Yuan, i.e., separately enacting a Commercial Registration Law for remedy, is that partners who register their names, addresses, and capital contributions with the official treasury shall be liable for losses based on their capital contributions. However, it has been stalled to this day due to inconsistent opinions of the Yuan committee. This meeting believes that the reasons stated in previous years' documents are extremely detailed and that another earnest conversation with the legislative authorities is necessary to bring the opinions into agreement. Therefore, today, we publicly visited President Sun of the Legislative Yuan to ask him to preside over the matter. In short, in recent years, in addition to occasional necessary matters communicated through official documents, there have been very few opportunities for daily contact between chambers of commerce, resulting in the loss of many opportunities for joint cooperation, which is regrettable. This meeting hopes that there will be opportunities for us to meet and exchange views often in the future and will take the National Anti-Smuggling Federation established this time as the starting point, thereby improving the All-China Federation of Chambers of Commerce. This level is the biggest gain of this session. On the day of the end of this session, I would like to add my wishes to this."

Reception and Tour

After the meeting, the representatives of the chambers of commerce from various provinces and cities, including Yu Rongqiao, were invited to visit the General Association for the Manufacture and Sale of Party and National Flags. We are determined to continue negotiations

The council is subject to the consular corps and cannot express dissent. It is reported that negotiations on the case have entered a standstill and will resume in the autumn. Raw Silk Quality Inspection

The Ministry of Industry ordered it to be launched as scheduled. The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry previously received an order from the ministry to prepare for the quality inspection of raw silk. As this matter is of great importance to the future of China's silk industry, a meeting of silk industry representatives from Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Sichuan, and Shandong provinces was convened last month to gather ideas and opinions. The results of the meeting were reported to the Ministry of Industry for verification. It has been learned that the bureau has received a telegram from Minister Wu, ordering the implementation of raw silk quality inspection from August 1 of this year and the mandatory implementation of grade inspection from February 1 of next year. All white filature silk trade exported from Shanghai shall be based on the results of the bureau's inspection. The grade standards shall be formulated by the bureau and submitted to the ministry for verification before the 15th of next month. It is scheduled to be announced on September 1. After receiving the telegram, the bureau has sent copies of the raw silk quality public weighing and inspection procedures and draft grade standards to the Shanghai, Wuxi, Zhejiang, Sichuan, and other silk factory trade associations for distribution to various silk factories for study. If there are any comments, they should be sent to the bureau by August 10 for reference and submission to the ministry for approval.

Doubts about Voucher Tax Stamps, Ministry of Finance Instructs Compliance

After the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance for instructions on how to affix stamp duty to payment vouchers, the association received a reply from the Ministry of Finance, Tax No. 10135, yesterday: "The telegram and attachments have been received in full. Upon investigation, the payment vouchers used by the Zhufeng Tongji Enamel Company, if used within the factory by various departments to receive the funds they need, or by factory staff to receive funds for petty expenses, should be considered for internal use and do not create external rights and obligations. Therefore, there is no need to affix stamp duty. However, when compiling them into a book, stamp duty of 20 cents should still be affixed according to the example of loose-leaf ledgers. If factory staff use this voucher to receive their salary, then the recipient should affix stamp duty according to the example of silver receipt. When compiling them into a book, there is no need to affix stamp duty again on the cover of the book according to the book example. As for this voucher, if it is given to people outside the factory to receive money, it belongs to the nature of the vouchers for withdrawing silver and money in item 4 of the tax rate table. The company should affix stamp duty according to law before delivery. When the recipient signs for receipt on the voucher, there is no need to affix stamp duty again. However, if the receipt is over 100 yuan, stamp duty of 1 cent should still be affixed by the recipient according to the provisions of the last paragraph of Article 8 of the Stamp Tax Law, which states that if the tax rates are different, the higher tax rate should be used. When compiling them into a book, there is no need to process them according to the book example again. This is for your compliance."

Public Works Department Health Authorities Discuss: Summer Heat Prevention Methods

Recently, this city has been hit by a heat wave, making the intense heat unbearable. Even sitting still indoors is difficult to breathe, and those walking in the scorching sun feel as if they are standing above a furnace. Cases of heatstroke and sudden collapse are common. The Public Health Bureau of the International Settlement has published information on how to combat the heat. Here is a translation of the key points, which we believe the public will find useful.

Although Shanghai's weather is often extremely hot in the summer, it is interspersed with occasional storms. Therefore, residents do not consider heat prevention methods to be essential. However, in near-tropical regions, everyone knows to study and follow methods of cooling down and seeking relief from the heat. Therefore, knowing some methods of preventing heat during hot days is an important aspect of summer health. There is much debate among doctors regarding sunstroke, heatstroke, and fainting, with no consensus. Some argue that the light rays in sunlight that can cause chemical reactions cannot penetrate the skull or spine. Therefore, what ordinary people call sunstroke does not scientifically exist, and sun hats, back coverings, and other sun protection items are unnecessary. Those who hold this view have medical evidence to support their claims, making it difficult for ordinary people to refute them. However, on the other hand, when a person is exposed to sunlight and suffers localized burns, in addition to local pain, the entire system of the body feels uneasy. Therefore, from the perspective of general public health, even if sunstroke has no basis in science, the invasion of sunlight must be prevented. This can not only prevent irritation of a part of the skin, but also prevent serious illnesses caused by excessive heat in the body.

Sun helmets can be used because they are thick and do not transmit heat. Black glasses are also necessary to protect the eyes. However, Easterners do not need dark crystal glasses as much as Westerners, because Westerners have light-colored retinas that are more susceptible to sunlight. Furthermore, the amount of moisture in the air is closely related to personal comfort. In drier air, sweat evaporates faster, so even if it is hot, it does not feel uncomfortable. Conversely, when the humidity reaches the saturation point, sweat does not evaporate easily, and one immediately feels stuffy. Therefore, one should be especially careful to prevent heatstroke on quiet, windless days or nights in the summer. Furthermore, according to the findings of an expert in India, rapid drops in temperature can also easily lead to heatstroke and sudden collapse. Sleeping well at night can increase physical strength and enhance the ability to resist heat the next day.

Often, when the body is subjected to prolonged heat, the mechanism in the nervous system that manages body heat becomes overwhelmed and unknowingly abandons its resistance work. As a result, the sweating and other mechanisms that maintain a normal body temperature break down. At this time, one feels hot all over but stops sweating, which is a warning sign of heatstroke and should be carefully prevented. However, heatstroke can also be caused by high humidity in the air, which prevents sweat from evaporating. Therefore, in factories, making the air dry and circulating is an urgent task in the summer.

In addition, there are several rules for individuals to follow in the summer to prevent heatstroke, issued by the health authorities of Pittsburgh, USA. Here is an excerpt: (1) Dress in loose, comfortable clothing; (2) Take extra care when moving from hot to cold places; (3) Drink plenty of cold (boiled) water; (4) Do not overeat; (5) Do not eat spoiled or unclean food; (6) Do not get angry; (7) Exercise moderately, but do not overexert yourself; (8) Seek balance in everything; (9) Wear a hat when going out; (10) Conserve physical, mental, and emotional energy. Whether drinking more water is beneficial depends on each individual's constitution. However, the Eastern proverb "Do not drink alcohol before the sun goes down" should be followed in the summer. During the hottest part of the day, muscles should be relaxed, and it is best to lie down in a cool room for a while, which also helps to increase resistance. Therefore, it is very beneficial to extend the lunch break in the summer.

In recent years, experiments in factories have shown that in hot and humid workplaces, workers who sweat profusely due to long hours of work lose salt in their bodies. Adding a small amount of salt to the drinking water can compensate for this. It is said that after adopting this method, workers feel much less sensitive to the heat. However, we must know that one person's food may be another person's poison. Whether adding salt to water is beneficial or harmful depends on the individual's constitution and may not be suitable for general use. Regarding clothing, summer is most difficult for men, as men's clothing, such as collars, belts, and sleeves, restrict them. Abandoning these restrictions is not yet the time, but the collar of the shirt should be chosen to be larger in size to make it comfortable and allow air to circulate. As for how clothing should be improved, that is another question.

The most enviable people in summer are women. Light silk and gauze are unnecessary to mention, but even a gauze dress is much better than men's clothing. Moreover, women stay indoors and are free to relax, unlike men who have to work for a living, and they can let the scorching sun bake them.

Cholera Prevention Office Announces: Cholera Prevention Steps

Living Conditions Are Very Important

The Shanghai Cholera Prevention Temporary Office announced yesterday the cholera prevention steps, saying that clean water supply, vaccination, food management, fly eradication, and personal hygiene are important for cholera prevention, but housing problems are also very important and should not be ignored. Poor people, without sanitation facilities, cannot understand the ways to health, and they still use dirty water from ditches for washing rice, vegetables, and utensils. In order to improve this kind of environment, the municipal government has built four model civilian villages in the city in the past three years. Each village has a square for citizens to rest. The rents of the houses are very cheap, ranging from 3 to 4 yuan, and most of them are rented to the working class. The locations of the civilian villages are Zhongshan Road, Pushan Road, Qimei Road, and Damuqiao Road. Compared with the needs of Shanghai citizens, this number is a small beginning.

Use Alcohol With Caution

Four People Have Died in the Last Two Weeks: Public Works Department Issues Warning

The Public Works Department's factory division recently issued a serious warning to all factories, large and small, that use alcohol. According to the division's report, in the past three weeks, there have been multiple explosions in factories in the International Settlement due to improper or negligent use of alcohol, resulting in the deaths of four workers and serious injuries to two others. One explosion occurred when welding a crack in a broken iron drum. The second explosion occurred when a burning cotton swab was carelessly thrown onto an alcohol can. Although the can had a lid, there were two small holes that leaked air. Another explosion occurred when pouring alcohol onto a fire. As for the fourth explosion, the circumstances surrounding the incident are unknown because two officials have died. What is known is that the explosion must have had a source of ignition, and alcohol vapor is extremely explosive. Factory owners must take precautions. Therefore, no matter how alcohol is used, attention should be paid at all times and in all places. Even empty cans that have contained alcohol should not be placed anywhere. When not in use, it is best to wash them clean with water and store them in one place to prevent residual alcohol from vaporizing and causing accidents. Sources of ignition should not be allowed near places where alcohol is stored. Extreme caution should be taken when welding broken cans or opening new cans. This applies not only to alcohol but also to sulfuric acid, alcohol, ether, and other dangerous substances. In recent years, there have been several major accidents caused by using blowtorches to open cans. Factory owners should provide guidance to workers at all times to teach them how to prevent various dangers.

After the trial, Xu Rengui was sentenced to fifteen years in prison, Zhang Xibiao and Jin Hongxiang were sentenced to ten years in prison each, Chen Jianzhao was sentenced to eight years in prison, Wang Shipin was sentenced to seven years in prison, Jin Zhoushi was sentenced to three years and six months in prison, Xi Xinquan and Ma Liangfu were sentenced to five years in prison each, Zhu Mingji was sentenced to three years in prison, and all were deprived of public rights for the duration of their sentences. Wang Xieshi was found not guilty. All details have been reported in this newspaper. It is learned that the two criminals, Xi Xinquan and Ma Liangfu, have been confirmed to have begun serving their sentences. Wang Xieshi was released because the police department did not appeal. The remaining seven criminals, Xu Zhangjin, Chen Xi, and Zhu Zhoushi, did not accept the judgment and appealed to the Third High Court. The court hearing was held the other morning by Judge Zhu Huanbiao, acting as presiding judge of the High Court, accompanied by Judges Wang and Liao and the prosecutor. Except for the husband and wife Jin Hongxiang and Jin Zhoushi, all of the appellants in the Police Department unanimously requested to withdraw their appeals in court. The court granted their request and ordered them to be sent to prison to execute the original sentence. The court then began hearing the appeal of the Jin couple, summoned the victim, the detectives in charge of the case, and the appellants who withdrew their appeals for questioning. After the police department's lawyer and the appellants' defense lawyers argued, the court announced the conclusion of the hearing and scheduled the judgment to be pronounced on the 25th. The appellants were remanded to custody.

Resisting Coffee and Cocoa

Tea Powder

Tea, as a beverage, is a major export of our country. In recent times, not only has the export volume of tea decreased sharply, but the import of beverages such as coffee and cocoa has increased daily, which is of great importance to the national economy and people's livelihood. Zhuang Wanfang and Dong Yiyun, in view of this, have jointly researched and produced a tea powder to replace coffee and cocoa. The fine powder is very similar to cocoa, and the granular powder is like coffee. It is said that the ingredients are similar to tea, but better than coffee. However, the aroma is not as strong as coffee and still needs to be improved. The fine powder is more suitable for manufacturing candy, ice cream, and milk blending raw materials. As for the equipment for manufacturing tea powder, it is still under research and design. It is also heard that in the future, this product will be sold exclusively by the most famous tea house, Wang Yutai.

Broadcasting Association News

The Shanghai Private Radio Broadcasting Industry Association, located at No. 323 Jiangxi Road, was previously ordered by the Telegraph Bureau to inform all broadcasters to submit their manuscripts to the Association for submission to the Telegraph Bureau for review in order to review broadcasting scripts. Now, because a small number of broadcasters directly submit them to the Telegraph Bureau, the Broadcasting Association has no way to verify them and will not be able to notify the member stations to comply. Therefore, a representative was sent to contact Shen Yide of the relevant department of the Telegraph Bureau, who has agreed to order all broadcasters to write four copies of the manuscripts, whether they are submitted to the Telegraph Bureau or the Association, so that one copy can be stored in the Association for verification. The total time for the ten restricted programs is three hours, except for the period from 7 pm to 10 pm every day. The previous report stated that the time was from 6 pm to 10 pm and the total amount was two hours, which was a misunderstanding. As for the rumor that a certain group in the ten restricted programs had asked the Association to forward a request to the Telegraph Bureau to cancel the restriction, the person in charge of the member station said that no group had contacted the Association, so he did not know about it.

Shanghai Consolidated Tax Inspection Office - Seized Cigarette Hand-Crank Iron Machines

Director Qian of the Consolidated Tax Bureau of the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui regions recently learned that private cigarettes were rampant in areas such as Yannan, Henan, Xuchang, and Xinyang. The hand-crank iron machines used were mostly smuggled by Shanghai merchants. Therefore, he secretly ordered the Shanghai Inspection Office to instruct all branch offices and patrol boats to strictly investigate. Cai Guanglu, the director of the Beishi Branch Office, after receiving the order, learned that merchants often smuggled iron machines through the North Station. In the 24th year, as many as eight units had been seized. Recently, because the station inspection was strict, it was not easy to slip through the net. The merchants disassembled the hand-crank machines into parts, packed them into postal packages, and sent them to those areas through the post office in the concession. As for machine parts, such as iron legs, they were transported by ships. In addition to reporting the investigation to the higher authorities, the Office also supervised the inspectors to step up the arrest. Yesterday morning, the branch office received a tip from an informant that Yongli Iron Factory had disassembled a hand-crank iron machine, mixed it with scrap iron, packed it into four bamboo baskets, and handed it over to Jielu Huitong Transportation Company, falsely claiming it was scrap iron, and entrusted the Road Bureau to transport it to Yancheng. According to the report, the Office immediately went with the informant and detained all four bamboo baskets. Together with Luo Guisheng, a reporting clerk of Huitong Company, they were taken to the Office. The bamboo baskets were opened, and the scrap iron was removed. Each basket contained new hand-crank iron machine parts at the bottom. They were assembled into a complete hand-crank iron machine on the spot. It was reported to the Shanghai Inspection Office for verification on the same day. According to the report, the Office immediately forwarded it to the Consolidated Tax Bureau of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui to be dealt with severely according to law, in order to serve as a warning.

Cai Huaiqing, an accountant from Ningbo, currently thirty years old, who works for Xiang Sheng Automobile Company, located at No. 800 Beijing Road, has been working for the company for more than two years. The company's general manager, Zhou Xiangsheng, sued Cai Huaisan (that is, Huaiqing's brother), Cai's guarantor, in the local court. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Criminal Court of the First Special Court. The company authorities suspected Cai's departure, and immediately started an investigation, only to find out that Cai had fraudulent accounts. The station then sent detectives to inquire at the defendant's residence at No. 122 Xiafei Road in the French Concession. His wife, Cai Hong, said that her husband had not returned for many days, so there was no result. Meanwhile, the company pursued the guarantor Cai Huaisan. It was not until this month that Manager Zhou returned to Shanghai and found out that the defendant entered Xiang Sheng Automobile Company as an accountant in January of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, specializing in managing the daily payments from various branches and customers' deposits and transferring them to the bank. Because the procedures were complicated, another person was assigned to help the defendant cooperate in April of this year. However, the defendant knew that he had used the accounts privately and could not hide it, so he had to run away. It was found that the defendant's method of fraud was to privately cancel the deposit of 10,000 yuan under the name of Mei and treat it as if it had been withdrawn. There were also more than 4,000 yuan of business payments from various branches, but the defendant only deposited 30,000 yuan into the bank. The two frauds totaled more than 11,000 yuan. After deducting more than 2,000 yuan that the defendant had already returned to the driver as a guarantee deposit, the actual amount of embezzlement was 8,540 yuan, etc. When questioned, the defendant Cai Huaiqing admitted that he had used the accounts privately for 8,540 yuan. After Judge Feng Shide verified the confession, he ruled that the defendant would be detained for another seven days for further questioning.
